тАШMaireyakaтАЩ is another reading for тАШMaitreyaka.тАЩ

тАШMadh┼лka-likeтАЩтАФThis word expresses a simile; it means that the man is тАШas sweet as the madh┼лka flower,тАЩ being possessed of a sweet voice. Or, it may mean тАШhe who behaves like the madh┼лka flowerтАЩ;тАФthe word being formed with the тАШDaтАЩ affix; and the elongation of the second vowel being one that is permitted in the case of several words; the elongation of the first vowel being due to the reflexive affix.

тАШWho praise men constantlyтАЩтАФand are called on that account тАШbards.тАЩ

тАШAt sun-riseтАЩтАФat the time of the rising of the sun,тАФthese people ring the bell; with a view to awaken the King and other rich men.

The caste here mentioned is begotten on the тАШ─АyogavaтАЩ woman,тАФshe being the woman mentioned in this connection.тАФ(33)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

In view of the term тАШon Vaideha womanтАЩ occurring later on (37), the meaning must be that тАШon the Vaideha woman, from the Niс╣г─Бda is born the K─Бr─Бvara.тАЩ

From the Vaidehaha are born the two castes тАШAndhraтАЩ and тАШMeda,тАЩтАФ on what women?тАФon the K─Бravara and the Niс╣г─Бda women respectively. That such is the meaning is implied by the fact of these two being the last spoken of. We explain the verse to mean this in view of the fact that an entirely different caste is born from the Vaideha father on a Vaideha mother. Thus then what is meant is that from the father of the same caste are born two different castes,тАФthis difference being due to the difference in the castes of the mothers.

тАШOutside the villageтАЩтАФ is their тАШdwelling,тАЩ livinghouse.тАФ(36)

тАШVyasanaтАЩ is suffering;тАФthe тАШm┼лla,тАЩ of it is killing; what is meant is that the livelihood of these men is the executing of criminals, the carrying of the dead bodies of men dying without any relations, the taking away of their clothes, eating the cakes offered to the dead, and so forth.

This caste is born from the тАШCaс╣Зс╕Н─БlaтАЩ on the тАШPukkasaтАЩ woman.

Or, тАШm┼лlaтАЩ may be taken as standing for the roots of trees, and the тАШvyasanaтАЩ would stand for the dissecting of these; and this forms their livelihood. That is, they live by selling the roots and other things extracted out of the trees that have been cut down.тАФ(38)

рд╕реНрд╡рдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрд╛рд╕реН рддреНрд░реИрд╡рд░реНрдгрд┐рдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрд╛рд╕реБ104 рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╕реН рддреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдг рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрддреН рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН рдПрд╡рд╛рдиреВрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рддреБрд▓реНрдпрддрд╛рднрд┐рдзрд╛рдирдВ рддрджреНрдзрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердореН ред рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рдЬрд╛ рдЕрдиреБрд▓реЛрдорд╛рдГ ред рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рддреН рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдпреЛрдГ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рджреН рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдГ, рддреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдг рдЙрдкрдиреЗрдпрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЙрдкрдиреАрддрд╛рд╢реН рдЪ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рдзрд░реНрдореИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░реН рдЕрдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪ “рддрд╛рдиреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдирд╛рдореНрдирдГ” (рдореНрдзреН резреж.резрек) рдЗрддрд┐ рдорд╛рддреГрдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН рдПрд╡ ред рддрддрд╢реН рдЪ рддрдЬреНрдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдореЗрд╖реБ рдзрд░реНрдореЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдПрд╡рд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред

  • рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдирд╛рдо рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд╛рдордЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрд╛рддреН рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮреИрд╡реИрд╖рд╛рдВ рди рддреБ рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрддрд┐рджреЗрд╢ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд╕реНрдпрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЖрд╢рдЩреНрдХрд╛ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрддрдГ рд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╖рдЯреН рд╕реБрддрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд┐рдгрдГ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рд░рдореНрднрдГ ред105 рдпреЗ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЕрдкрдзреНрд╡рдВрд╕рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрдХрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реН рддреЗ рд╢реВрджреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рд╕реН рддрджреНрдзрд░реНрдореИрд░реН рдЕрдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд▓реЛрдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рддреБ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЛ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН рдЕрдиреБрд▓реЛрдореЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдПрд╡ ред рддреЗрди рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд┐рддреЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рджреН рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рддреЛ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╖рдЯреНрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд┐рд░рд┐рдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рди рд╢реВрджреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рд░рд╢рд╡рдГ рее резреж.рекрез рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

From тАШtwice-bornтАЩ persons, sons born of women of the same caste as themselves belong to the same caste; and all these тАШpartake of the character of twice-born personsтАЩ;тАФthis is the reiteration of a well-known fact And the assertion that sons born of women of the next lower caste also stand on the same footing is made for the purpose of indicating that the same rights and privileges belong to those also.

тАШThose born of women of the next lower casteтАЩтАФi.e., in the тАШnatural orderтАЩ; of those born to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa father and the Kс╣гatriya or Vai┼Ыya mother, or those born to the Kс╣гatriya father from the Vai┼Ыya mother.

These тАШpartake of the character of twee-born personsтАЩтАФi.e., they should have the Initiatory Rite performed for them, and having become initiated, they become entitled to all that pertains to a twice-born person.

тАЬIt has been declared under 14 above that тАШthey are called by the name of the next lower caste,тАЩ which means that all such sons of the natural older belong to their motherтАЩs caste; so that it would naturally follow that they are entitled to all that pertains to that caste.тАЭ

True; but since the passage referred to uses the term тАШname,тАЩ people might have the idea that the sons are only so by name, and not by caste; hence with a view to make the point dear, we have another assertion in the present text, which asserts that тАШthe six sons partake of the character of twice-born men.тАЩ

Those sons however who are born of тАШviolationтАЩтАФi.e., of a mixture of the castesтАФтАШare of the nature of ┼Ъ┼лdras,тАЩтАФi.e., having the character of the ┼Ъ┼лdra, they are entitled to the rights and duties of that caste.

The peculiarity in connection with sons born in the тАШinverse orderтАЩ is going to be described later on. The term тАШnext lower CasteтАЩ in the present text has been added only for the purpose of indicating that what is said here applies to the sons of the тАШnatural orderтАЩ only. So that the son born to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa from a Vai┼Ыya women, who is one step removed from the тАШnext lower casteтАЩтАФalso becomes included. But, the number being limited to тАШsix,тАЩ the son bora to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa from the ┼Ъ┼лdra woman,тАФi.e., тАШP─Бra┼ЫaraтАЩтАФis not included here.тАФ(41)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШThis verse is quoted in Vyavah─Бra-B─Бlambhaс╣нс╣н─л (p. 570).

B├╝hler

041 Six sons, begotten (by Aryans) on women of equal and the next lower castes (Anantara), have the duties of twice-born men; but all those born in consequence of a violation (of the law) are, as regards their duties, equal to Sudras.

042 рддрдкреЛ-рдмреАрдЬ-рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡реИрд╕реН рддреБ ...{Loading}...

рддреЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреБрдЧреЗ рдпреБрдЧреЗ ред
рдЙрддреНрдХрд░реНрд╖рдВ рдЪрд╛рд╜рдкрдХрд░реНрд╖рдВ рдЪ
рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрд╖реНрд╡реН рдЗрд╣ рдЬрдиреНрдорддрдГ рее резреж.рекреи рее

рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╖реН рдЯреАрдХрд╛рдГ ...{Loading}...
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

By the force of austerities and the seed they attain higher or lower rank among men, through birth, cycle after cycle.тАФ(42)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдд рдПрддреЗ рд╜рдирдиреНрддрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рддрдкрдГрд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпреЗрди рдмреАрдЬрд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпреЗрди рдпреБрдЧреЗ рдпреБрдЧреЗ рдЬрдиреНрдордирд┐ рдЬрдиреНрдордирд┐ рдЙрддреНрдХрд░реНрд╖рдореН рдЕрдкрдХрд░реНрд╖рдВ рдЪ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрджреН рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдордГ “рд╢реВрджреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдЬреН рдЬрд╛рддрдГ” (рдореНрдзреН резреж.ремрек) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рее резреж.рекреи рее

рдпрджреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН “рд╕реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗрди” (рдореНрдзреН резреж.реирек) рдЗрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡рд╛рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдГ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШTheyтАЩтАФi.e., the sons born of the next lower castes,тАФтАШby the force of austeritiesтАЩ and тАШby the force of seedтАЩ;тАФтАШcycle after cycle,тАЩтАФi.e., in each successive birth;тАФтАШattain higher or lower rank.тАЩ

All this is going to be described under verse 64 et. seq.тАФ(42)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШYuge yugeтАЩтАФтАШIn successive birthsтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi, N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana);тАФтАШin each of the ages of the worldтАЩ (Kull┼лka).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

┼Ъukran─лti (4.4, 80-81).тАФтАШVi┼Ыv─Бmitra, M─Бtaс╣Еga, Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha, N─Бrada and others became elevated by special penances, not by birth.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (1.96).тАФтАШCaste becomes elevated during the fifth or the seventh generation; similarly after five or seven generations one acquires that caste of which he has followed the occupations.тАЩ

Gautama (4.22-24).тАФтАШIn the seventh generation, men obtain a change of caste, being either raised to a higher one or degraded to a lower one. The venerable teacher declares that this happens in the fifth generation, and the same rule applies to those born from parents of different castes that are intermediate between two of the castes originally created by Brahm─Б.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (2, 11.10-11).тАФтАШIn successive births, men of the lower castes are born in the next higher one, if they have fulfilled their duties. In successive births, men of the higher castes are born in the next lower one, if they have neglected their duties.тАЩ

042 By the power of austerities and of the seed (from which they sprang), these (races) obtain here among men more exalted or lower rank in successive births.

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рд▓реЛрдкреЛ рдпрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрддрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдмрдзреНрдпрддреЗ, рдпрдереЛрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ,106 рдпрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрддреГрддрдпрд╛, рдпрдерд╛ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╕рдВрдзреНрдпреЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ ред рддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рд▓реЛрдк рдЙрднрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдирдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдореН ред рдЕрддрд╢реН рдЪ рди рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдореН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗрди рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рднреНрд░рдВрд╢рдГ, рдЕрдкрд┐ рддреВрдкрдиреАрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣ рд╢рдирдХреИрд░реН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╕рдВрддрддреЗрдГ рдкреНрд░рднреГрддрд┐ рд╢реВрджреНрд░рддреНрд╡рдореН, рди рддреБ рдЬрд╛рддрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡107 ред рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗ рддреБ рддрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡ рд╡реНрдпрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╕рд╛ рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рд░реН рди рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рддрддреНрдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рднреГрдЬреНрдЬрдХрдгреНрдЯрдХрд╛рджрд┐рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдПрд╡ рд╡реНрдпрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╣реЗрддреБрдХрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдгреЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╕рдВрд╢рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреНрддреЗ рд╡рд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рд╖рджреНрдЧрдордирд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее резреж.рекрей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Now follow the details regarding тАШthe omission of oneтАЩs dutiesтАЩ spoken of above.

тАШOmission of sacred ritesтАЩтАФ This includes the rites that are done for the person, such as Initiation and the rest, as also those that he does himself, such as the Agnihotra, the Twilight Prayers and so forth. And the тАШomissionтАЩ of these is the non-performance of both these sets of rites. Thus one loses his caste not only by the omission of the Initiatory Rite, but also by the neglecting of those that have been enjoined as to be done after the Initiation.

This is what is meant by тАШgraduallyтАФwhich means that the continued neglect of the rites reduces successive generations to the position of the ┼Ъ┼лdra; and this does not refer to the new-born child, who loses his title only by the omission of his Initiation.

It is not that the manтАЩs caste becomes lost; all that happens is that he becomes liable to be called by such castes-names as the тАШBhс╣Ыjjakaс╣Зс╣нakaтАЩ and the rest.

тАШBy the neglect of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas,тАЩтАФi.e., by transgressing the injunctions pertaining to Br─Бhmaс╣Зas. Or it may refer to not consulting the Council of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas in doubtful matters arising out of the scriptures, in regard to expiatory rites and other cognate matters.тАФ(43)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtattva II (p. 268) to the effect that even in in modern times Kс╣гatriyas can become degraded to ┼Ы┼лdrahood.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 10.43-44)
**

Mahabharata (13.33.21-22; 13.35.17-18).тАФтАШ┼Ъ─Бkas, Yavanas, K─Бmbojas and other Kс╣гatriya castes became degraded by not seeing the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas. Dr─Бviс╕Нas, Kaliс╣Еgas, Pulindas, U┼Ы─лnaras, Kolisarpas and M─Бhiс╣гakas and other Kс╣гatriya castes became degraded by not seeing the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas. Kir─Бtas, Yavanas and other Kс╣гatriya castes became degraded because they would not bear with the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.тАЩ

┼Ъukran─лti (4.4.74).тАФтАШThe Yavanas have all the four castes mixed together; they recognise authority other than the Vedas and live in the North and West. Their ┼Ъ─Бstras have been framed for their welfare by their own teachers.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШPuс╣Зс╕НraтАЩтАФand the rest originally stood as names of countries; but in the present context they have been used according to the theory that тАШthese names really denote the particular Kс╣гatriya castes, and are only indirectly applied to countries inhabited by them.тАЩ

P─Бс╣Зini 4.2.69 lays down the adding of the тАШaс╣ЗтАЩ affix in the sense of habitation, and S┼лtra 4.2.81 lays down the elimination of this affix; it is in accordance with this that we have the form тАШPuс╣Зс╕НraтАЩ (which is formed of the term тАШpuс╣Зс╕НraтАЩ with the тАШaс╣ЗтАЩ affix);тАФand the elimination is not according to P─Бс╣Зini 1.2.54.

The assertion that these people have become тАШlow-bornтАЩ is based upon the fact that in these countries we do not meet with any dear division of the тАШfour castes.тАЩ

If however these terms be tried to be used irrespectively of the names of countries, then they should be taken as the names of so many castes.

Some people might be led to think that all these races here named are found to be described as Kс╣гatriyas, so that they must be Kс╣гatriyas still. And it is with a view to preclude this idea that it is asserted that these are low-born.

All the people here spoken of form the races inhabiting the borders of ─Аry─Бvarta,тАФsuch races for instance, as the Kir─Бta, the тАШVenaтАЩ, the тАШDaradaтАЩ and so forth; and it is with reference to this that we have the declaration that тАШone should not go to the bordersтАЩ (Bс╣Ыhad─Бraс╣Зyaka Upaniс╣гad, 1.3.10).тАФ(44)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

That language is called тАШmlecchaa,тАЩ тАШbarbaric,тАЩ which consists of words that either have no meaning, or have a wrong meaning, or are wrong in form. To this class belong the languages of such low-born tribes as the ┼Ъabara, the Kir─Бta, and so forth.

тАШRefined languageтАЩ is the language of the inhabitants of ─Аry─Бvarta.

These persons, being other than those named as the тАШfour castes,тАЩ are called тАШDasyu.тАЩ

The meaning is that neither habitation nor barbaric speech is a ground for regarding a caste as тАШmixedтАЩ; it is the fact of people being known by the particular names that makes them to be so regarded. It is thus that they come to be called тАШDasyu.тАЩтАФ(45)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШDwellingтАЩтАФliving place; this should be far removed from the village.

тАШApap─Бtra,тАЩтАФ(a) Kept aloof; the vessels in which they have eaten shall not be cleaned for further use; they shall be thrown away; with the exception of gold and silver vessels, in connection with which special methods of cleaning have been prescribed.

(b) Or, the term тАШApap─БtraтАЩ may mean that when cooked rice, fried flour or some such food is given to them, they shall not be given in vessels that are in contact with their body; the food shall be given into the vessel lying on the ground, or held in the hand by some one else, and when the vessel thus filled has been placed on the ground, it shall be taken away by them.

(c) Or again, тАШApap─БtraтАЩ may mean broken vessel; as it is going to be asserted (in the next verse) that тАШthey shall eat in broken dishes.тАЩ

тАШTheir wealth shall consist of dogs and donkeysтАЩтАФThey shall not receive cows or horses, or gold and silver, as their wealth.тАФ(51)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЕрдиреБрдкрд╕реНрдХреГрддреЛ рдзрдирдореН рдЕрдЧреГрд╣реАрддреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрднреНрдпрд╡рдкрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЕрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ ред рдмрд╛рд╣реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд▓реЛрдорд╛рдирд╛рдореН ред рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдгрдореН рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдЬрд╛рддреМ рдЬрдиреНрдорд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреЗрдГ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рд╣реЗрддреБрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН123 рдПрд╡рдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рдЬрдиреНрдо рд▓рднрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрдерд╛рдзрд┐рдХреГрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╛рджрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд░реН рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдГ рее резреж.ремреи рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШUnrequitedlyтАЩтАФwithout: receiving any reward.

тАШDefenceтАЩтАФfavour.

тАШAliensтАЩтАФchildren born in the тАШinverse order.тАЩ

тАШPerfection is securedтАЩ;тАФthe attaining of a superior caste is called тАШperfection,тАЩ on the ground of its leading up to it; the meaning being that these people come to be born in a caste where they become entitled to the rights and responsibilities of the higher caste.

Or, тАШperfectionтАЩ may stand for the attaining of heaven.тАФ(62)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Mah─Бbh─Бrata (13.48.34-35).тАФтАШRendering help to cows and Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, and practising sympathy, mercy, truthfulness, forgiveness and protecting others even by oneтАЩs own body,тАФthese are the means of success for outcasts.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (16.18).тАФтАШGiving up life, regardless of any reward, in order to save a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, or a cow, or for the sake of a woman or a child,тАФmay confer heavenly bliss even upon members of the base castes.тАЩ

B├╝hler

062 Dying, without the expectation of a reward, for the sake of Brahmanas and of cows, or in the defence of women and children, secures beatitude to those excluded (from the Aryan community, vahya.)

рдЙрдкрдпреЛрдЧрдГ, рди рд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рдХрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХреЛ рдЬреАрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рди рдШрд╛рддрд╛рджрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рддрдиреНрддреНрд░рдореН рее резреж.ремрей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШPurityтАЩтАФrefers to external purity, brought about by the use of clay, water and such things.

тАШSum, and substance.тАЩтАФThis means that this is what pertains to entire human community, and not only to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and the other castes.

The rest has been already explained.

тАЬIf тАШabstention from injuring creaturesтАЩ is the duty of the mixed castes of the тАШinverseтАЩ order, how is it that it has been declared thatтАФтАШkilling fish is the livelihood of the Niс╣г─БdasтАЩ (48), тАШand the catching of animals,тАЩ living undergroundтАЩ (49), and тАШthe killing of wild animals for the Kс╣гattс╣Ы and others?тАЩтАЭ

In answer to this some people offer the explanation that the тАШabstention from injuringтАЩ refers to injury other than that which has been prescribed as oneтАЩs livelihood.

Others think that what is here meant is that тАШabstention from injuryтАЩ is that kind of duty which is the source of spiritual welfare, and it does not mean the absolute prohibition of all injury. Just As it is in the case of the assertionтАФтАШthere is no harm in the eating of meat etc., etc.тАЩ

тАЬIf тАШabstention from injuryтАЩ is a duty, how are the men to subsist? Other sources of income being not available to them, and abstention from injury being regarded sis conducive to spiritual welfare, what would be their means of livelihood? Specially as all other professions have been restricted to each distinct caste. For instance, teaching and other similar professions; are absolutely impossible, and cannot be available; agriculture and cognate professions are restricted to Vai┼Ыyas; and service is the exclusive duty of the ┼Ъ┼лdra.тАЭ

How these men are to subsist we shall explain below, under 116. It is further stated (in 46) that тАШthey shall subsist by doing undespised manual labour for the twice-born peopleтАЩ; and what could be more тАШdespisedтАЩ than injuring living beings? As for the тАШkilling of fish,тАЩ this could be of no use to twice-born men? It is true that an occasional use for it has been spoken of in connection with ┼Ъr─Бddhas and the reception of guests; but that could not serve as a permanent means of livelihood.

From all this it follows that no one is free to do any killing or injuring of living beings.тАФ(63)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (1.122).тАФтАШAbstention from injury, Truthfulness, Abstention from theft, Purity, Control of the senses, Liberality, Self-control, Mercy, Tolerance,тАФthese are the means of righteousness for all men.тАЩ

Vy─Бsa (Apar─Бrka, p. 164).тАФтАШFreedom from cruelty, Abstention from injury, Kindness, Liberality, Performance of ┼Ъr─Бddha, Honouring guests, Truthfulness, Freedom from anger, Contentment with oneтАЩs own wife, Purity, Freedom from envy, Self-knowledge and Patience are the common virtues…… Truth, Self-control, Austerity, Purity, Contentment, Shyness, Tolerance, Straightforwardness, Wisdom, Calmness, Mercy, Concentrated mindтАФthese constitute the eternal Dharma.тАФThat is Truth which is beneficial to living beings; Self-Control consists in controlling the mind; Austerity consists in remaining firm in oneтАЩs own duty; Purity consists in the evading of inter-mixtures; Contentment consists in giving up objects of sense; Shyness consists in desisting from evil deeds; Tolerance consists in the capacity to bear the pairs of opposites; Straightforwardness consists in balance of mind; Wisdom consists in discerning the true nature of things; Calmness consists in peacefulness of mind; Mercy consists in the inclination to do good to living beings;тАФthis is eternal Dharma.тАЩ

Bс╣Ыhaspati (Do.).тАФтАШMercy, Tolerance, Freedom from envy, Purity, Abstention from over-exertion, Propitiousness, Freedom from miserliness, Freedom from desires,тАФthese are common to all men.тАФWhen one protects another person in times of trouble,тАФwhether he be a stranger or a relation, an enemy or a friend,тАФthis is what is meant by Mercy. Tolerance is that by virtue of which one does not become angry on suffering pain. When one does not feel unhappy at the good qualities of another, and eulogises even those whose qualities are not of the best;тАФthis is called Freedom from envy. Purity consists in avoiding forbidden food and in associating with blameless persons. When one avoids those acts which, though good, bring suffering to the body, that is Abstention from over-exertion. Propitiousness consists in doing what is good and desisting from what is not commended. Freedom from Miserliness is that by virtue of which one gives away, without pain, even the little that he possesses. Freedom from Desires is that by which one remains contented with whatever he obtains, without thinking of what others have got.тАЩ

Gautama (8.22-23).тАФтАШNow follow the eight qualities of the soulтАФCompassion on all creatures, Forbearance, Freedom from anger, Purity, Quietism, Propitiousness, Freedom from avarice and Freedom from covetousness.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (1.23-6).тАФтАШFreedom from anger, from exultation, from grumbling, from covetousness, from perplexity, from hypocrisy and hurtfulness,тАФTruthfulness, Moderation in eating, Silencing slander, Freedom from envy, Self-denying, Liberality, Avoiding of gifts, Uprightness, Affability, Extinction of the passions, Subjugation of the senses, Peace with all beings, Concentration of mind, Regulation of conduct according to the ─Аryas, Peacefulness and Contentment;тАФthese good qualities have been settled by the agreement of the wise for all the four orders. He who, according to the precepts of the sacred Law, practises these, enters the Universal Self.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (2.16-17).тАФтАШForbearance, Veracity, Restraint, Purity, Liberality, Self-control, Avoiding the killing of animals, Obedience to elders, Pilgrimage, Sympathy with the afflicted,тАФStraightforwardness, Freedom from covetousness, Reverence towards God and Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, and Freedom from anger are duties common to all.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The offspring here referred to (though mentioned by a masculine noun) stands for the child in general, just as in the case of such assertions as тАШgarbhe gс╣Ыhс╣З─Бс╣нi,тАЩ тАШgorbhe j─Бtaс╕етАЩ and so forth. The sense of the verse thus comes to be this:тАФтАШA maiden born from a ┼Ъ┼лdra woman to a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa father,тАФif she is тАШwedded toтАЩтАФacquires the capacity for bearing children, by becoming conjoined in wedlock toтАФa person of a superior caste i.e., the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa,тАФand the girl born of this maiden is again married to a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa,тАФand this goes on for seven generations, then in the seventh generation, the child that is born becomes a regular Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.тАЩ

Though the text speaks of the тАШsuperior casteтАЩ in general, yet it should be taken as meaning that the ┼Ъ┼лdra attains the position of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa; and this because the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is mentioned in the text, and also because the next verse speaks of the ┼Ъ┼лdra attaining the position of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.

On the principle enunciated here, the child born from the Vai┼Ыya mother (and the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa hither) attains the superior caste in the fifth generation; and that born from the Kс╣гatriya mother, in the third generation.

In all these cases the тАШsuperiorityтАЩ is in comparison to the caste of the mother. So that if the girl born to a Vai┼Ыya father from a ┼Ъ┼лdra mother is married to a Vai┼Ыya, she attains the superior caste in the third generation; and the girl born of the ┼Ъ┼лdra mother to the Kс╣гatriya hither, on marrying the Kс╣гatriya, acquires the higher caste in the fifth generation. The term тАШyugaтАЩ here stands for birth, generation.

The тАШinferiorтАЩтАФone belonging to a lower casteтАФattains the тАШsuperiorтАЩтАФthe higher caste.

The article тАШ─БтАЩ (in the expression тАШ─Б saptam─БtтАЩ) indicates limit.тАФ(64)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

If the daughter of a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa from a ┼Ъudr─Б female and all their descendants marry Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, the offspring of the sixth female descendant of the original couple will become a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa (Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka and R─Бghav─Бnanda).тАФIf the son of a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa from a ┼Ъ┼лdra female marries a similar girl possessed of excellent virtues and if his descendants go on doing the same, the child born of the sixth generation will become a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana)

Gautama (4.22).тАФтАШIn the seventh generation, men obtain a change of caste, either being raised to a higher, or degraded to a lower one.тАФThe venerable teacher declares that this happens in the fifth generation.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

That тАШthe ┼Ъ┼лdra attains the position of the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩ is what, has already been asserted above.

тАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa sinks to the position of the ┼Ъ┼лdraтАЩ.тАФThe тАШBr─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩ meant here should be understood to be the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa-born тАШP─Бr─Б┼Ыatra.тАЩ If he marries a ┼Ъ┼лdra girl of the nature described above, he sinks down to the lower level, in the third generation. This is how they explain this.

People who attain the higher caste, according to the principle here enunciated, become entitled to the sacraments and rites pertaining to that caste.тАФ(65)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШWhichтАЩтАФdenotes question.

If the тАШseedтАЩ forms the more important factor, the children born from mothers of lower castes gradually attain the higher caste of the father; and the same principle might be applied to the case of the тАШsoilтАЩ being regarded as the more important factor. So that, just as the child born to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa father from a тАШNon-Aryan,тАЩтАФi.e., ┼Ъ┼лdraтАФmotherтАФтАШsome-howтАЩтАФi.e., even when the woman is not his married wife,тАФwould attain the higher casteтАФso also тАШthe child born to a non-Aryan from the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa womanтАЩ would attain the higher caste, on the ground of the тАШsoilтАЩ being the more important factor;тАФit having been declared (under 9.34) that тАШpredominance attaches sometimes to the seed and sometimes to the soilтАЩтАФ (66)

тАШAn─Бry─Бy─БmтАЩтАФтАШA ┼Ъ┼лdra femaleтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka, R─Бghav─Бnanda and Nandana);тАФтАШthe daughter of a Vr─Бtya and the likeтАЩ (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa).

рдПрд╡рдВ рдЪ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШWomanтАЩтАФfemale.

тАШNon-─АryaтАЩтАФbelonging to a low caste.

тАШTo an ─АryaтАЩтАФto one belonging to a high caste.

Such a person would be an ─Аrya.

тАЬDoes he actually become a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa?тАЭ

No; he is an тАШ─АryaтАЩ only тАШin quality,тАЩтАФonly figuratively; i.e., only so far as being entitled to the performance of the P─Бkayaj├▒a rites.

This person is called an тАШ─АryaтАЩ only in comparison with the person going to be described in the latter half of the text.

тАШOne born to a non-─БryaтАЩтАФa ┼Ъ┼лdraтАФтАШfrom an ─Аrya womanтАЩтАФa Br─Бhmaс╣Зa femaleтАФтАШis always non-─БryaтАЩ.

This is the decision.

The meaning of all this is that the pre-eminence of any mixed caste is to be accepted only in accordance with what is distinctly stated in the text, and no inferences should be drawn regarding this matter. Hence the right course would always be that one should have intercourse with a woman of the same caste as himself; and what is said regarding the^(тАШ)soilтАЩ being the important factor, pertains only to the case of the^(тАШ)soil-bornтАЩ son, and not to any other cases.тАФ(67)

067 The decision is as follows: ‘He who was begotten by an Aryan on a non-Aryan female, may become (like to) an Aryan by his virtues; he whom an Aryan (mother) bore to a non-Aryan father (is and remains) unlike to an Aryan.’

рдпрдерд╛ рддреНрд░рдп рдПрддреЗ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ ред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рдкрдХреНрд╖рдГ рдХреЗрдирдЪрд┐рддреН рдкрд░рд┐рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдГ ред рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЖрд╣реБрд░реН рдмреАрдЬрдореН рдПрд╡ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдЬреН рдЬрд╛рддрдГ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рдорд╛рддреГрдЬрд╛рддрд┐рдд рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдГ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЖрд╣реБрдГ- рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардореН, рдпрддрдГ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛ рдпрддреНрд░реЛ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░реЗ рдЬрд╛рддрдГ рддрдЬреНрдЬрд╛рддреАрдпреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐, рддрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡ рдЪ рддрджрдкрддреНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдкрд░реЗ рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ- рдЙрднрдпреЗ рдмреАрдЬрдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░реЗ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реА ред рддрджреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН “рд╕реБрдмреАрдЬрдВ рдЪреИрд╡ рд╕реБрдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░реЗ” (рдореНрдзреН резреж.ремреп) рдЗрддрд┐ ред

  • рддрджреН рдПрддрддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд░реЛрдЪрдпрдорд╛рди133 рдЖрд╣- рддрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдВ рддреБ рд╡реНрдпрд╡реНрд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рдГ ред рдЗрдпрдореН рдЕрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рд░реВрдкреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдореН рее резреж.ренреж рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

There are three theories, each being held by some sage or the other.

(1) Some people assert that the тАШseedтАЩ is the more important factor; so that the child born to a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa from a woman of the Kс╣гatriya or other castes, is superior to his motherтАЩs caste.

(2) Others declare the тАШsoilтАЩ to be the more important; whence the тАШsoil-bornтАЩ son belongs to the caste of the mother from whom he is born, and to whom he belongs.

(3) Others again hold that both are equally important; as declared in 69тАФтАШas good seed sown in good soil etc, etc.тАЩ

Not satisfied with any of these views, the Author addsтАФтАШThe decision on this point is as follows;тАЩтАФi. e., after full consideration the following decision has been arrived at.тАФ(70)

рдирд╛рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкреНрдпрддреЗ рд╜рднрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╡рддреН ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рдПрд╡реИрддреЗ рее резреж.ренрей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШNon-─Бrya,тАЩтАФ ┼Ъ┼лdra.

тАШBehaving like an ─Аrya,тАЩтАФdevoted to the service of twice-born men, performing the P─Бkayaj├▒a sacrifices, always respectful towards Gods and Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.

тАШ─АryaтАЩтАФBr─Бhmaс╣Зa and the rest.

^(тАШ)Behaving like a non-─Бrya,тАЩтАФdoing what is forbidden and omitting what is enjoined.

Having тАШexamined these two,тАЩтАФi.e., having considered their relative merits; having pondered over the question whether the one or the other was superior in his qualities,тАФPraj─Бpati, Manu, made the declaration.

^(тАШ)They are not equal.тАЩтАФInasmuch as тАШcasteтАЩ is the most important factor, the ┼Ъ┼лdra, even though possessed of superior merit, can never be equal to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.

He said againтАФ^(тАШ)they are not unequalтАЩ;тАФfor though of superior caste, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is beset with many defects.

The meaning of all this is that no man can be respected simply on the strength of his caste; what wins respect is quality; if one is devoid of good qualities, his caste cannot come to his rescue; for if it did, then there would be no point in the prescribing of expiatory rites.

[From verse 66] to the present one, the text is intended to be a deprecation of the тАШconfusion of castes,тАЩ and the praise of the due performance of oneтАЩs duties; there is nothing either enjoined or forbidden, nor is anything new asserted. Hence all these verses should he taken as purely commendatory.

073 Having considered (the case of) a non-Aryan who acts like an Aryan, and (that of) an Aryan who acts like a non-Aryan, the creator declared, ‘Those two are neither equal nor unequal.’

This is meant to serve as an introduction to the subject of тАШDuties in abnormal times.тАЩ

тАШYoniтАЩ is source, birth.

Br─Бhmaс╣Зas of pure Br─Бhmaс╣Зa-birth should perform the six acts:тАФthe root тАШupa-j─лvaтАЩ denoting performance here.

тАШIn due orderтАЩтАФin accordance with their rights and capacities; i.e., each one doing the act to which he is entitled.

Some of the acts serve spiritual purposes, while others fulfill only material purposes.тАФ(74)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШBrahmayonisth─Бс╕е.тАЩтАФтАШIntent upon the source of the VedaтАЩ(Medh─Бtithi),тАФтАШIntent upon the means of union with BrahmanтАЩ (Kull┼лka);тАФтАШof pure Brahmanical raceтАЩ (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and R─Бghav─Бnanda);тАФтАШwho abide by what springs from the Veda, i.e. the sacred law,тАФor who are the abode of the VedaтАЩ (Nandana).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (2.13-14).тАФтАШThe lawful occupations of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa are six: studying the Veda, teaching, sacrificing for himself, sacrificing for others, giving gifts and accepting gifts.тАЩ

Gautama (10.1-3).тАФтАШThe lawful occupations common to all twice-born men areтАФstudying the Veda, offering sacrifices for themselves and giving gifts.тАФTeaching, offering sacrifices for others and accepting gifts are the additional occupations for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.тАФBut the former three are obligatory.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (1.18.2).тАФтАШBrahman forsooth, placed Its majesty in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, together with the duties and privileges of studying, teaching, sacrificing for themselves, sacrificing for others, giving gifts and accepting gifts,тАФfor the protection of the Vedas.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (2.10.4-5).тАФтАШThe lawful occupations of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa areтАФstudying, teaching, sacrificing for himself, sacrificing for others, giving gifts, receiving gifts, inheriting and gleaning corn in the fields; and he may live by taking other things that belong to nobody.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (2.5, 9, 11).тАФтАШFor a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, to teach the Veda,тАФto sacrifice and to study the Veda,тАФfor a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, to sacrifice for others and to receive gifts.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (1.118).тАФтАШSacrificing, studying and giving gifts are common to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya; for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa there are in addition to these, accepting gifts, sacrificing for others and teaching.тАЩ

┼Ъukran─лti (4.3.31-32).тАФтАШSacrificing, studying, giving gifts,тАФthese are the functions of the twice-born;тАФthe additional special functions of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa areтАФreceiving gifts, teaching and sacrificing for others.тАЩ

K─Бmandaka (2.18-19).тАФтАШThe celebration of sacrifices, the study of the Vedas, and the giving away of wealth to others, according to the rules of the ┼Ъ─Бstras,тАФthese are considered to be the common customary observances of the three castes, Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, Kс╣гatriya and Vai┼Ыya.тАФThe holy acts of teaching, of conducting sacrifices for others, and of accepting gifts from the piousтАФthese have been enumerated by the sages to be the means of livelihood for those belonging to the highest caste.тАЩ

Artha┼Ы─Бstra (p. 29).тАФтАШThe special duty of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is to study, to teach, to sacrifice for himself, to sacrifice for others, to give gifts and to receive gifts.тАЩ

074 Brahmanas who are intent on the means (of gaining union with) Brahman and firm in (discharging) their duties, shall live by duly performing the following six acts, (which are enumerated) in their (proper) order.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

These were mentioned under Discourse I, only with a view to eulogising the Treatise; on the present occasion they are mentioned for being enjoined. Though the injunction of each of them singly has already gone before, yet, in a friendly spirit, the author, sets them forth here collectively. And as this statement is dependent upon other injunctions, it is to be taken as reiterating what has Been enjoined before, for the purpose of introducing the forthcoming injunction.тАФ(75)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The division of the functions into groups of three is for a distinct purpose. One group of three has been put forward as serving (temporal) ends, while the other is conducive to invisible (spiritual) ends.

тАШPureтАЩтАФ Not. addicted to sinful deeds.

тАЬBut the ┼Ъ┼лdra also could be pure.тАЭ

Why should you have an aversion to that.?

тАЬIt would he contrary to other Smс╣Ыti texts, where it is laid down that тАШthe Br─Бhmaс╣Зas feed at the house of, and receive gifts from, such twice-born persons as are praiseworthy for their actions.тАЩ In face of this the present text should be explained in such a manner as to avoid the contradiction of those other texts. For so long as a reconciliation of varying texts is possible, it is not right to admit of such contradiction.тАЭ

As a matter of fact, the present text is merely reiterative; the real injunction having gone before, in such texts asтАФтАШhe shall seek to obtain wealth from Kс╣гatriyas, etc., etc.тАЩ (4.33).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in. Madanap─Бrij─Бta, (p. 215);тАФin Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б, (1.118) to the effect that three out of the six functions are conducive to merit and these are to be practised as means of livelihood; so that while the former are obligatory, the latter are not so;тАФin Par ─Б ┼Ыaram ─Б dhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 140), to the same effect;тАФin Vyavah─Бra-B─Бlambhaс╣нс╣н─л, (p. 424);тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 122).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

These three functions, which are the means of livelihood, do not belong to the Kс╣гatriya; but those that are conducive to spiritual endsтАФi.e., studying and the rest,тАФdo not cease.

Inasmuch as the Veda is the subject-matter in consideration, it is the teaching of the Veda that is forbidden for the Kс╣гatriya, and not that of the science of archery and other arts and sciences.тАФ(77)

Gautama (10.1, 7, 15, 49).тАФтАШThe occupations common to all the twice-born areтАФstudying, offering sacrifices, and giving gifts,тАФto protect all beings is the additional function of the king (Kс╣гatriya), and to learn the management of chariots and the use of the bow;тАФthe additional occupations of the Vai┼Ыya are agriculture, trade, cattle-tending, and money-lending.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (1.18.3, 4).тАФтАШIn the Kс╣гatriya, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa placed strength, together with the duties and privileges of studying, sacrificing, giving gifts, using weapons and protecting the life and property of all beings,тАФfor the growth of good government.тАФIn the Vai┼Ыyas, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa placed the power to work, with the duties of studying, sacrificing, giving gifts, cultivating the soil, trading, and cattle-tending,тАФfor the growth of productive labour.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (2.10.6, 7).тАФтАШThe lawful occupations of the Kс╣гatriya are the same as those of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa; with the exception of teaching, sacrificing for others and receiving gifts; and with the addition of governing and fighting. The lawful occupations of the Vai┼Ыya are the same as those of the Kс╣гatriya, with the exception of governing and fighting, and with the addition of agriculture, cattle tending and trade.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (2.15-19).тАФтАШThe lawful occupations of the Kс╣гatriya are threeтАФstudying, sacrificing for himself and bestowing gifts;тАФand his peculiar duty is to protect the people with his weapons; he may earn his livelihood by that means.тАФThe lawful occupations of the Vai┼Ыya are the same besides agriculture, trading, cattle-tending and money-lending.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (2.6, 7, 9, 12, 13).тАФтАШFor the Kс╣гatriya, constant practice in arms;тАФfor the Vai┼Ыya, the tending of cattle;тАФfor all the twice-born, to sacrifice and to study;тАФthe mode of livelihood for the Kс╣гatriya is to protect the world (and receive due reward);тАФand for the Vai┼Ыya, tillage, keeping cows, trade, money-lending and growing of seeds.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (1.118, 119).тАФтАШSacrificing, studying and giving gifts are common to the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya (and the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa);тАФthe principal function of the Kс╣гatriya is the protecting of the people; money-lending, agriculture, and trade and cattle-tending are the principal functions of the Vai┼Ыya.тАЩ

┼Ъukran─лti (4.3.33-34).тАФтАШThe additional special functions of the Kс╣гatriya are the protection of the good, suppression of the wicked and realising of revenues. The additional functions of the Vai┼Ыya are agriculture, pasture and trade.тАЩ

K─Бmandaka (1.20).тАФтАШThe King (Kс╣гatriya) should live by his weapons and by protecting the people. The means of subsistence for the Vai┼Ыya are cattle-rearing, agriculture and trade.тАЩ

Artha┼Ы─Бstra (p. 29).тАФтАШThe duties of the Kс╣гatriya are studying, sacrificing, making gilts, living by arms, and protecting of living beings; of the Vai┼ЫyaтАФstudying, sacrificing, giving gifts, agriculture, cattle-tending and trade.тАЩ

B├╝hler

079 To carry arms for striking and for throwing (is prescribed) for Kshatriyas as a means of subsistence; to trade, (to rear) cattle, and agriculture for Vaisyas; but their duties are liberality, the study of the Veda, and the performance of sacrifices.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШVedic studyтАЩ.тАФSince the subject-matter of the section is the means of livelihood, this must be taken as standing for the teaching of the Veda.

тАШThese are the most useful among their respective occupations.тАЩ That is, among the means of livelihood sanctioned by the scriptures for them, these are most conducive to their welfare, out of all the other occupations carried on for the purpose of livelihood.тАФ(80)

080 Among the several occupations the most commendable are, teaching the Veda for a Brahmana, protecting (the people) for a Kshatriya, and trade for a Vaisya.

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдпрджрд╛рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд░реАрд░рдХреБрдЯреБрдореНрдмрдирд┐рддреНрдпрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рд╡рд╕рд╛рджреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐, рди рддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкрд░реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдВ145 рдзрдирдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐, рддрджрд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрдиреН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрдереЛрдХреНрддреЗрди рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ ред рддрджрд╛ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╡рддреН рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордирдЧрд░рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдзрд╛рд░рдгреЗрди, рд╕рддрд┐ рд╕рдВрднрд╡реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзрд┐рдкрддреНрдпреЗрди рдЬреАрд╡реЗрддреН ред рдЬреАрд╡рддрд┐рд░реН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рд░реНрдердГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╕рдВрдзрд╛рд░рдгреЗ рди рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐, рдХреБрдЯреБрдореНрдмрд╕реНрдп рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рдореН146 рдЕрдкрд┐ рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐ ред рд╕ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдирдиреНрддрд░рдГ ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░ рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдирдиреНрддрд░рдГ ред рд╣реЗрддреБрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рджреН рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд┐рддрдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ рдкрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рд░реА ред рее резреж.реорез рее

рд╕реНрд╡рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдиреИрд╡рдВ рдордиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдордХреГрддрд╕реН рддрддреНрд░ рди рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╢реВрджреЗрд╖реНрд╡реН рдЕрдкреАрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

When ho finds it difficult to maintain himself, his family and his business, and he is unable to obtain wealth sufficient for all this, then he is said to be тАШunable to subsist.тАЩ

тАШAs described aboveтАЩ;тАФi.e., by Teaching and the rest Ho may make, like the Kс╣гatriya, a living by guarding over villages and towns, by carrying arms and weapons, and also, if possible, by ruling over the people.

The exact meaning of тАШmaking a livingтАЩ has been already explained; it does not stand here for the mere maintenance of oneтАЩs own body; it implies the maintenance of the family and also the carrying on of oneтАЩs business.

тАШHe is next to himтАЩтАФтАШpratyanantaraтАЩ is the same as тАШanantara.тАЩ Inasmuch as the text has provided this reason, it follows that the occupations of those removed by further degrees (i.e., of the Vai┼Ыya or the ┼Ъ┼лdra) involve sin for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa. Though the abandoning of his own occupation would be the same in all, yet it should not be thought that there is no difference in the degree of transgression of the law involved in having recourse to the occupations of the Vai┼Ыya and those of the ┼Ъ┼лdra; since, as the next verse declares, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa may have recourse to the occupation of the Vai┼Ыya).тАФ(81)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 231);тАФin V─лramitrodaya, (R─Бjan─лti, p. 13), to the effect that Kingship is not altogether forbidden to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa;тАФand in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (─Аhnika, 36b).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 10.81-84)
**

Gautama (7.4-7).тАФтАШIn times of distress, it is permissible to offer sacrifices for men of all castes, to teach them and to accept gifts from them; each preceding mode of living being preferable to the succeeding. On failure of the occupations lawful for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, he may live by the occupations of the Kс╣гatriya; and on failure of these latter, he may live by the occupations of the Vai┼Ыya.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (1.4.16-21).тАФтАШA Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, who is unable to subsist by teaching, sacrificing for others or the acceptance of gifts, shall maintain himself by following the duties of the Kс╣гatriya, because that is the next following caste. Gautama declares that the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa shall not act thus; for the functions of the Kс╣гatriya are too cruel for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa. They quote also the following verse:тАФтАЬOut of regard for the sacred law, a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa or a Vai┼Ыya may take up arms for the protection of cows or Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, or when a confusion of castes threatens to take place.тАЭ Or, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa may adopt the Vai┼ЫyaтАЩs means of livelihood; because that is the one following next. If he lives by agriculture, he shall plough before breakfast, and with two bulls whose noses have not been pierced, never striking them with the goad, but frequently coaxing them.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (2.22-24, 32-33).тАФтАШThose who are unable to live by their own lawful occupation may adopt that of the next inferior caste; but never that of a higher caste. A Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and a Kс╣гatriya who have resorted to the Vai┼ЫyaтАЩs mode of livelihood and maintain themselves by trade shall not sell the following thingsтАФstone, &c., &c., &c. For the purpose of cultivation, he shall plough before breakfast with two bulls whose noses have not been pierced; if he ploughs in the hot season, he shall water his beasts even in the morning.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (2.15).тАФтАШIn times of distress, each caste may follow the occupation of that next to it in rank.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (3.34).тАФтАШIn times of distress, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa may maintain himself by the occupation of the Kс╣гatriya, or by that of the Vai┼Ыya; but having tided over the distress, he shall purify himself by expiations and confine himself to his own path.тАЩ

Mah─Бbh─Бrata (3.208.23тАФ12.263.44-45).тАФ(Same as Manu 84.)

N─Бrada (1.56-60).тАФтАШIn times of distress, a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is allowed to gain his subsistence in the mode prescribed for the caste next to him in rank; or he may gain his subsistence like a Vai┼Ыya. But he must never resort to the mode of livelihood prescribed for the lowest caste. At no time should a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa follow the occupations of a man of vile caste, or a vile man the occupations of a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa; in either case, expulsion from caste would be the immediate consequence… When a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa has lived through the times of distress, with the wealth acquired by following the occupations of the Kс╣гatriya, he must perform a penance and relinquish those occupations. When a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa takes delight in those occupations and persists in them, he is declared to be a K─Бс╣Зс╕Нapс╣Ыс╣гс╣нha and must be expelled from society, because he has swerved from the path of duty.тАЩ

рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдордХреБрдЯреБрдореНрдмрд╛[рд╡]рд╕рд╛рджреЗ рдЕрдпрдореН рдЕрдЬреАрд╡рдиреН рднрд╡рддрд┐, рдпрддрдГ рдПрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдпрд╛рдореН рдЙрддреНрд╕реГрдЬреНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдо рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордирдЧрд░рджреЗрд╢рд╛рджреН - рд░рдХрд╖рдгрдореН (?) рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЕрдкрд░реЗ рддреНрд╡реН рдПрдХрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрддреНрдерд╛рдиреЗрди рд░рд╛рдЬрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЖрд╣реБрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдирдиреНрддрд░рд╣реЗрддреБрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рджреН рдЕрд╕реНрдпреЗрд╖рддреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рдпрддрд╛ рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ ред рдХреНрд░рдорднреЗрджреЗ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рдпрдЧреМрд░рд╡рдореН рее резреж.реорез рее

B├╝hler

081 But a Brahmana, unable to subsist by his peculiar occupations just mentioned, may live according to the law applicable to Kshatriyas; for the latter is next to him in rank.

  • рддрддреНрд░ рдХреГрд╖рд┐рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬреНрдпрдХреБрд╢реАрджрд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрдирд╛рдкрджреНрдпреН рдПрд╡реЛрдХрд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╛рджрд┐рд╡рддреН, “рдкреНрд░рдореГрддрдВ рдХрд░реНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╕реНрдореГрддрдореН ред рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдиреГрддрдВ рддреБ рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬреНрдпрдореН” (рдореНрдзреН рек.релтАУрем) рдЗрддрд┐147 рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЖрд╣реБрдГ ред “рдХреГрд╖рд┐рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬреНрдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВрдХреГрддреЗ,148 рдХреБрд╕реАрджрдВ рдЪ” (рдЧреНрдзреН реп.релтАУрем) рдЗрддреБ рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВрдХрд░рдгрдореН рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рднреНрдпрдиреБрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрддреЗ ред
  • рдпрддреН рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╛рджрд┐рд╡рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдореНрдпрдореН рдЖрд╢рдЩреНрдХрд┐рддрдореН, рдЕрддреНрд░реИрд╡ рдкрд░рд┐рд╣реГрддрдореН ред рдпрджрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдХреГрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╕рдорддреНрд╡реЗрди рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ, рдХрдердореН рдЗрджрдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ “рд╡рдгрд┐рдХреНрдкрд╢реБрдХреГрд╖реАрд░реН рд╡рд┐рд╢рдГ рдЖрдЬреАрд╡рдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН” (рдореНрдзреН резреж.ренреп) рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдпреЛрд░реН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдирд╛рдЬреАрд╡рдирд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реН рддрджрд╛ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдЪ “рдпрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдиреЗ рдЪреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╢реБрджреНрдзрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ” (рдореНрдзреН резреж.ренрем) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рддрд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╕рдорд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдпрддреН ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреН рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╛рджрд┐рдирд┐рдпрдореИрд░реН рдЬреАрд╡рддрдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛ рдПрд╡ ред рдпрд╕реН рддреБ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░рдгрд╛рджреН рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреНрд░реИрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдГ рд╕ рддрддреНрд░реИрд╡ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рддрдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЬрдирдГ рее резреж.реореи рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШIf he is unable to subsist by these two occupations.тАЩ The text is meant to lay clown a distinct order of sequence; at first he is to adopt, the occupation of the caste next to him, and then that of the caste removed a degree further.

The mention of тАШagriculture and cattle-tendingтАЩ is meant to stand for all the occupations of the Vai┼Ыya. That is why trading is also permitted, in view of which the author is going to forbid (in 85, et. seq.) the selling of certain things by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.

тАШHe may live the living of the Vai┼ЫyaтАФThe two acts (denoted by the terms тАШliveтАЩ and тАШlivingтАЩ) are spoken of as cause and effect,тАФone standing for the general act of living, and the other for the special forms of living.

Some people have held that from among the occupations of the Vai┼Ыya, agriculture, trade, and money-lending have been permitted (for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa) even during normal times,тАФjust like Teaching and other occupationsтАФunder verses 4.5 and 6. In Gautama (10.5 and 6) also we readтАФтАШAgriculture and trade done by himself, as also money-lendingтАЩ; which permits the carrying on of agriculture and trade by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa himself.

As for the view that these stand on the same footing as Teaching and other occupations (of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa himself),тАФthis has been refuted by us already. If agriculture and other occupations of the Vai┼Ыya stood for all three castes, on exactly the same footing,тАФthen, why should тАШtrade, cattle-tending and agricultureтАЩ have been mentioned as the most useful occupation тАШfor the Vai┼ЫyaтАЩ (verse 79)? And for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and the Kс╣гatriya also, these should not have been mentioned as to be adopted only under the stress of want of livelihood; in fact they should have been mentioned along with тАШTeaching, sacrificing for others and receiving gifts from pure menтАЩ (76) [which have been mentioned as the special occupations of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa].

The conclusion therefore is that so long as the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa can make a living by teaching and the other occupations laid down for himself, agriculture and the rest are forbidden to him. As regards the texts (4. 5 and 6) permitting these latter for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the real meaning of this we have already explained under those texts.тАФ(82)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa thinks that тАШKс╣Ыс╣гiтАЩ means here that agriculture whereat the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa himself does not do any manual work; bat Govindar─Бja and Kull┼лka reject this view.

This verse is quoted in Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б, (3.35), to the; effect that in abnormal times for purposes of livelihood the Br ─Бh maс╣Зa may have recourse to the functions of the Vai┼Ыya, but never to those of the ┼Ъ┼лdra;тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta, (p. 232);тАФand in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (─Аhnika, 36b).

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдХреГрд╖рд┐рдВ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╛рджреНрд╡реН рдПрд╡ рдХрд░реНрдо рдЗрддрд┐ рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рддрджреН рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН150 ред рдХрд░реНрд╖рддрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕реНрдп рдмрд╣реБ рдзрд╛рдиреНрдпрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐, рддрддреЛ рд╜рддрд┐рдереНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рднреНрдпреЛ рд╜рдиреНрдирджрд╛рдиреЗрдиреЛрдкрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐, рдЕрддрдГ рд╕рд╛рдзреНрд╡реА ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪреЛрдХреНрддрдореН “рдирд╛рдХреГрд╖реНрдпрддреЛ рд╜рддрд┐рдерд┐рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ” ред “рдХреГрд╖рд┐рдВ рдпрддреНрдиреЗрди рдХреБрд░реНрд╡реАрдд рдореМрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдпрддреНрдирддрдГ” ред рддрдерд╛ “рд▓рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд▓рдВ рдкрд░реАрд░рд╡рдВ рд╕реБрд╢реЗрд╡рдВ рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рддреНрд╕рд░реБ ред рдЙрджрд┐рддреН рдХреГрд╖рддрд┐ рдЧрд╛рдореН рдЕрд╡рд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рдлрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдкреАрд╡рд░реАрдореН” (рддреНрд╕реН рек.реи.рел.рем) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ ред

  • рддреЗ рди рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рд╕рд╛ рд╣рд┐ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕рджреНрднрд┐рд░реН рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдХрд╕реНрдп рд╣реЗрддреЛрдГ ред рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдореН рдЕрдпреЛрдореБрдЦрдВ рд▓рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд▓рдореН ред рднреВрдорд┐рд╢рдпрд╛рдВрд╢реН рдЪ ред рднреВрдореМ рд╢реЗрд░рддреЗ рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╕реН рддреГрдгрдЬрд▓реВрдХрд╛рджрдпрд╕реН рддрд╛рдВрд╢реН рдЪ рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪ рднреВрдореЗрдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рд╣рдирдирдВ рди рд╣рд┐ рд╕рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рд╡рддреН рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╣рддреНрдпрд╛рдкреАрдбрд╛рдореН151 рдЕрдиреБрднрд╡рддрд┐ ред

  • рдЕрдиреБрднреВрддрдВ152 рддреБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░реН153 рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рднреВрдореЗрд░реН рджреЛрд╖рд╡рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рее резреж.реорек рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

People think agriculture to be a good occupation; one who carries on agricultural operations obtains much grain, whereby he feeds guests; that is why it is тАШgood.тАЩ To the same end we have such assertions asтАФтАШHe who does not till the ground is not loved by his guests,тАЩ тАШone should carefully carry on agricultural operations,тАЩ and тАШthe plough, the spear, tills the soil etc., etc.,тАЩ (V─Бjasaneya Saс╣Гhit─Б, 12.71)

This view however is not the right one to take. This is an occupation that is despised by the righteous;тАФand the reason for this lies in the fact that тАШthe iron-tipped woodтАЩтАФthe ploughтАФтАШinjures the Earth and the earthly creatures,тАЩтАФi.e., those creatures that live under the ground, e.g., the caterpillar and the rest.

тАЬWhat sort of injury is inflicted on the Earth? The Earth certainly does not suffer pain, like the living creatures, by the stroke of the wooden implement.тАЭ

What the text means is that the Earth does suffer pain, and thereby forbids all tearing of the ground.тАФ(84)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 426);тАФand in Apar─Бrka, (p. 937) as supplying the reason for forbidding land-cultivation by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.

084 (Some) declare that agriculture is something excellent, (but) that means of subsistence is blamed by the virtuous; (for) the wooden (implement) with iron point injuries the earth and (the beings) living in the earth.

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЗрджрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢рдГ рдкрдгреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЯреНрдкрдгреНрдпрдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрджреНрд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░реЗрдпрдВ рддрджреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд╡реИрдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рджреН154 рдзрдирд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреН155 рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗрди рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░реЗрдпрдореН ред рдЙрджреНрдзрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгреНрдпреН рдЙрджреНрдзрд╛рд░рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрдиреЛрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЙрджреНрдзреГрдд рдЙрджреНрдзрд╛рд░реЛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рддрджреН рдПрд╡рдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгреНрдпреН рдЕрдд рдЙрджреНрдзреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░реЗрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрд╡рд░реНрдзрдирдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдзрдГ156 ред рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╣рд┐ рдзрдирд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛ ред рддреНрдпрдЬрддреЛ рдзрд░реНрдордиреИрдкреБрдгрдВ рдзрд░реНрдореЗ рдпрд╛ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдард╛ ред рдЕрддрд╕реН рддреЗрди рдкрдгреНрдпрд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рдпреЛ рди рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддрд╢реН рдЪреЗрджрдореН рдЕрд╡рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ- рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╡реГрддреНрддреАрдирд╛рдВ рдЧрд░реНрд╣рд┐рддрд╛ рдХреГрд╖рд┐рдГ, рддрддреЛ рдиреНрдпреВрдирд╛ рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬреНрдпрд╛,157 рддрддреЛ рдЧреЛрд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрдпрдГ158 рее резреж.реорел рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШThisтАЩтАФrefers to what follows.

тАШSuch commodities as are sold by Vai┼Ыyas.тАЩтАФIf the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa has no wealth, he may, if pressed for livelihood, sell such things as are permitted to be sold by Vai┼Ыyas.

тАШExceptions.тАЩтАФThis term stands for the commodities excluded. тАШWith certain exceptionsтАЩ;тАФfrom which certain articles are excluded. The Br─Бhmaс╣Зa may sell the things, with the exception of those hereinafter enumerated.

тАШFor increasing his wealth.тАЩтАФThis describes the nature of things; it being well known that trade is conducive to increased wealth.

тАШRenounces the strictness concerning his duties,тАЩтАФi.e., his strict regard for his duty. This implies that as a rule the said selling should not be done; and the upshot of all this is that from out of the several occupations of the Vai┼Ыya, Agriculture is the worst for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, then trade, and then cattletending and the restтАФ(85)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 10.85-93)
**

Gautama (7.8-15).тАФтАШGoods not to be sold by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa areтАФperfumes, flavouring substances, prepared food, sesamum, hempen and linen cloth, skins, garments dyed red or washed, milk and preparations of it, roots, fruits, flowers, medicines, honey, flesh, grass, water, poisons, animals for slaughter; nor under any circumstances, human beings, heifers, female calves, cows big with young. Some declare that traffic in land, rice, barley, goats, sheep, horses, hulls, milch cows and draught oxen is also forbidden.тАЩ

─Аpastamba (1.20.10-13).тАФтАШTrade is not lawful for a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa;тАФin times of distress he may trade in lawful merchandise, avoiding the following, that are forbiddenтАФmen, condiments and liquids, colours, perfumes, food, skins, heifers, glueing substances, water, young corn-stalks, substances from which spirituous liquor is extracted, red and black pepper, corn, flesh, arms, and the hope of reward for meritorious deeds. Among the various kinds of grains, he shall specially not sell sesamum or rice.

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (3.6-38).тАФтАШFruits, stones, linen, Soma, human beings, cakes, plants, sesamum, rice, liquids, curds, milk, clarified butter, water, arms, wine, wax, honey, lac, grass, clay, skins, flowers, blankets, hairs, Takra, poisons, land, silken cloth, indigo, salt, one-hoofed animals, lead, vegetable, pepper, medicines, oil-cake, animals, perfumes,тАФthese the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should never sell, even when living by the occupations of the Vai┼Ыya. But sesamum may be sold for religious purposes, in exchange of paddy.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (2.2.27-29).тАФтАШHe who sells sesamum, forsooth, sells his ancestors; he who sells rice, forsooth, sells his life; he who gives away his daughter, making a bargain, forsooth, sells portions of his spiritual merit. Grass and wood in their natural state may be sold. They quote the followingтАФтАЬAnimals that have only one row of teeth, as well as minerals excepting salt, and undyed thread,тАФthese, O Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, are the goods thou art permitted to sell.тАЭтАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (2.24-31).тАФтАШA Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and a Kс╣гatriya, who have resorted to a Vai┼ЫyaтАЩs mode of living and maintain themselves by trade, shall not sell stones, salt, hempen cloth, silk, linen and skins; nor any kind of dyed clothing; nor prepared food, flowers, fruit, roots, perfumes, substances (used for) flavouring (food); nor water, the juice extracted from plants; nor Soma, weapons, poison, nor flesh, nor milk, nor preparations of it, iron, tin, lac, and lead. Now they quote also (the following verse): By (selling) flesh, lac, and salt a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa at once becomes an outcast; by selling milk he becomes (equal to) a ┼Ъ┼лdra after three days. Among tame animals those with uncloven hoofs, and those that have an abundance of hair (must not be sold), nor any wild animals, (nor) birds, nor beasts that have tusks (or fangs). Among the various kinds of grain they mention sesamum (as forbidden). Now they quote also (the following verse)тАФIf he applies sesamum to any other purpose but food, anointing and charitable gifts, he will be born again as a worm and, together with his ancestors, be plunged into his own ordure.тАФOr, at pleasure, they may sell (sesamum), if they themselves have produced it by tillage.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (54.18-21).тАФтАШHe who sells fresh ginger, edible plants, perfumes, flowers, fruits, roots, skins, canes, things made of split bamboo, chaff, potsherds, hair, ashes, bone, cow-milk or curds, oil-cakes, sesamum or oil, must perform the Pr─Бj─Бpatya. He who sells the fruit of the ┼Ыle┼Ыm─Бtaka tree, lac, bees-wax, shells, mother-o-pearl, tin, lead, iron, copper, or sacrificial vessels made of rhinocerosтАЩ horn, must perform the C─Бndr─Бyaс╣Зa. He who sells dyed cloth, tin, precious stones, perfumes, sugar, honey, liquids or condiments, or wool must fast for three days. He who sells meat, salt, lac or milk must perform the C─Бndr─Бyaс╣Зa. And all these persons should undergo initiation a second time.тАЩ

рднрд╛рд░реБрдЪрд┐рдГ

рдзрд░реНрдордиреИрдкреБрдгрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рджреН рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╣реАрдирддрд╛ рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ рдЧреЛрд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдЪ рд╕рддрд┐ рдХреНрдЯреНрд╖реЗрд░реН рд╡рд╛рдирд┐рдЬреНрдпрдореН рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдореН ред рддрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рдЧреЛрд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдВ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдп рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрддреН рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реЛ рд╜рдпрдореН рдЕрдзреБрдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЯреНрдкрдгреНрдпреЛрджреНрдзрд╛рд░ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдкрдгреНрдпрдореН рее резреж.реорел рее

He shall avoid all savoury substances as also cooked food and sesamum, stores, salt, animals and human beings.тАФ(86)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдордзреБрд░рд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╖рдбреН рд░рд╕рд╛рдГ ред рддрддреНрдкреНрд░рдзрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдЧреБрдбрджрд╛рдбрд┐рдордХрд┐рд░рд╛рддрддрд┐рдХреНрддрдХрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд┐рд╖рд┐рдзреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рди рд╣рд┐ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд░рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рдГ ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд░рд╕рд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рди рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпреЗ рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрд╡рджреН рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреНрдпреЗрди, рддрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН, “рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдШреЛрд╖рдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛159 ред рдЕрдкреЛрд╣реЗрдд рддреНрдпрдЬреЗрддреН, рди рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░реАрдгреАрдпрд╛рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН ред рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреНрдирдВ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН рдУрджрдирд╛рджрд┐ рддрдгреНрдбреБрд▓рд╛рджрд┐ рди160 ред рддрд┐рд▓реИрдГ рд╕рд╣, рддрд┐рд▓рд╛ рдЕрдкрд┐ рди рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░реЗрдпрд╛рдГ ред рди рддреБ рдкреБрдирд╕реН рддрд┐рд▓рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреНрдирдпреЛрдГ рд╕рд╣рдкреНрд░рдпреБрдХреНрддрдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ, рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдпреЛрд░реН рдЕрднреНрдпрдиреБрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН ред рдЕрд╢реНрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдГ ред рд▓рд╡рдгрдореН рдЕрдкрд╛рд╖рд╛рдгрд░реВрдкрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ ред рд╕реИрдиреНрджрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд╖рд╛рдгрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН ред рд░рд╕рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд▓рд╡рдгрд╕реНрдп рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрде рдЖрд░рдВрдмрдГ ред рддреЗрди рдордзреБрд░рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рдпрдГ ред рдкрд╢рд╡реЛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдпрд╛ рдЖрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖рд╛ рдореМрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рее резреж.реорем рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

There are six flavours, rasas,тАФsweet and the rest; and the term тАШrasa,тАЩ тАШsavoury substancesтАЩ here stands for substances abounding in one or other of these flavours; such as sugar, pomegranate, the тАШkir─Бta,тАЩ the тАШtiktakaтАЩ and so forth; all these are forbidden; and not only those that are made of the juices extracted from the trees etc., (which is the literal meaning of тАШrasaтАЩ). Though the term тАШrasaтАЩ is not used directly in the sense of substance, in the way in which тАШwhiteтАЩ and such terms are, yet it indirectly indicates it; just as in the case of the expression тАШthe ranch on the Gaс╣Еg─Б,тАЩ (the term тАШGaс╣Еg─БтАЩ indicates the river-bank).

тАШShall avoidтАЩтАФshall give it up; i.e., shall not sell.

тАШCooked foodтАЩтАФsuch as rice cooked and ready for being eaten.

тАШAnd sesamum.тАЩтАФSesamum also shall not be sold; and it is not meant that what is forbidden is such food as is cooked with sesamum, and the selling of each separately is permitted.

тАШStonesтАЩтАФOf all kinds.

тАШSaltтАЩтАФEven those that are not in the form of stone (solid); rock-salt being already included under тАШstones.тАЩ

If the term тАШrasaтАЩ is understood in its literal sense, of the six flavours, then, since тАШsaltтАЩ will have been already included under this, the separate mention of тАШsaltтАЩ would mean that the selling of this is absolutely forbidden for all time, while that of тАШsweetтАЩ and the rest is only partially so.

тАШAnimalsтАЩтАФ Tame as well as wild.

тАШHuman beingsтАЩтАФ Men.тАФ(86)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta, (p. 232), which explains тАШvyapohetaтАЩ (which is its reading for тАШapohetaтАЩ) as тАШshould avoidтАЩ i.e. тАШshould not sellтАЩ; it adds that тАШrasaтАЩ having been already mentioned, тАШlavaс╣ЗaтАЩ is mentioned again for the purpose of indicating that the selling of salt is more blameworthy.

тАШRaktaтАЩтАФi.e., red; the word тАШraktaтАЩ is known as denoting the red colour more than the others; e.g., it is only the ruddy bull that is called тАШrakta.тАЩ Though what the root тАШra├▒jтАЩ (to dye) denotes is only the imparting of some sort of colour to what is white.   • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рдорд╛рдзреНрд╡реАрдХрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡рд╛рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдорджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдордзреБрд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдгрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред

  • рддрджреН рдЕрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдирд╛рдпрдВ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкреАрдбрд┐рддрдореГрджреНрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд╕рд╡рдЪрдирдГ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐, рдорджреНрдпрд░реВрдкрддрдпреИрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред “рдЙрднреМ рдордзреНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╡рдХреНрд╖реАрдмреМ” (рдореНрднреН рел.релрео.рел) рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рддреН, рдХреНрд╖реАрдмрддрд╛ рдорджреНрдпрдХреГрддреИрд╡ ред рдЧреБрдбрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╕рддреНрд╡рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН162 ред

  • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рдЦрдгреНрдбрдорддреНрд╕реНрдпрдгреНрдбрд┐рдХрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреБрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ рее резреж.реорео рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШWeaponsтАЩтАФSwords, nooses and so forth.

тАШPerfume.тАЩтАФ Such special fragrant substances as the тАШTagara,тАЩ the тАШU┼Ы─лraтАЩ, Sandalwood and so forth; the term тАШgandhaтАЩ being explained in the same manner as the word тАШrasaтАЩ above.

тАШMilkтАЩтАФEverything made of milk, as described in other тАШSmс╣Ыti textsтАЩ such as sour cream, whey, co-agulated milk and so forth;тАФall these should not be sold. тАШCurdтАЩ and тАШbutterтАЩ have been mentioned separately with a view to indicate the special importance of these among all milkтАФproducts.

тАШMadhuтАЩ stands for тАШmadh┼лcchiс╣гс╣нaтАЩ bees-wax,тАФthe part (тАШmadhuтАЩ) standing for the whole тАШmadh┼лcchiс╣гс╣нa.тАЩ Just as тАШdevaтАЩ is generally used for тАШdevadatta.тАЩ That this is so follows from the fact that it is the selling of the тАШbees-waxтАЩ that is expressly forbidden in another Smс╣Ыti; and as for honey (Madhu) itself, it is forbidden in the present text by the special name тАШKс╣гaudraтАЩ,тАФthe grape-juice (which also is called тАШkс╣гaudra,тАЩ being expressly forbidden in a later verse under the name тАШmadya.тАЩ

Others however explain the term тАШmadhuтАЩ in the present verse as standing for grape-juice before fermentation has set in and it has become тАШwine,тАЩ тАШmadya.тАЩ

This however is not right. Because the word тАШmadhuтАЩ is not denotative of the freshly extracted grape-juice; in fact it always stands for it in the form of wine; as we find in such passages as тАШUbhau madhv─Бsavakс╣гibau,тАЩ where intoxication is spoken of as brought about by тАШmadhu,тАЩ and it is only wine that brings about intoxication.

тАШSugarтАЩ.тАФThis has been mentioned with a view to show that the prohibition of this could not come under that of тАЬr asaтАЩ (under 86). Others however explain that this has been added with a view to imply that the selling of things made of sugarтАФsuch as sweetmeatsтАФis permitted.тАФ(88)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

The second half of this verse is quoted in Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б (3.38), which adds the following notes:тАФтАШDadhi and kс╣г─лraтАЩ stand for all preparations of milk and curd; тАШghс╣ЫtamтАЩ for all oily substances;тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 232), which adds that тАШkс╣гaudramтАЩ stands for bees-wax, honey itself being mentioned separately (тАШmadhuтАЩ);тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 123).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

[Under 86], the selling of тАШcooked food and sesamumтАЩ has been forbidden; and to this the present verse is an exception, in view of certain special conditions and purposes.

тАШPure,тАЩ тАШnot kept longтАЩ;тАФthese refer to the condition of the grains; and тАШfor sacred purposesтАЩтАФrefers to the purpose.

тАШPure тАЩтАФ тАШnot mixed with Vr─лhi and other grains. There is possibility of mixed sesamum being sold for the purposes of preparing тАШmixed food.тАЩ

тАШNot kept long.тАЩтАФThis implies that the man shall not keep back the grains with the idea that they are selling cheap now, but after a few days they shall fetch higher prices.

Or, тАШpureтАЩ may mean not black; the prohibition applying to black sesamum; and sesamum becomes black if kept for a long time. The meaning is that he shall not sell black sesamum after having grown or bought it.

тАШThe agriculturist,тАЩ тАШif he has cultivated it himself.тАЩ These words are only descriptive, and much significance is not meant to be attached to them.

The selling of grains obtained in gifts is also not forbidden.

тАШFor moved purposes.тАЩ For instance, when sesamum is sold for the purpose of obtaining money whereby to buy the cow to be given as a sacrificial fee, or when it is sold for the performance of Vedic study, Agnihotra and such rites, or when it is sold for the purpose of buying with the price thus obtained, Vr─лhi and other corns needed for the performance of the Dar┼Ыap┼лrс╣Зam─Бsa and other sacrifices. In all these cases the selling is тАШfor a sacred purposeтАЩ;тАФor, when the sesamum itself is used by the purchaser for such religious acts as making gifts, or for getting oil for medicinal purposes.тАФ(90)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШ┼Ъuddh─БnтАЩтАФтАШunmixedтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka and R─Бghav─Бnanda);тАФтАШwhiteтАЩ (Nandana);тАФтАШof good qualityтАЩ (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa).

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 431) as permitting the selling of sesamum. It notes on this point two viewsтАФ(a) that what is said here refers to exchanging, and (b) that it permits the selling only for the purpose of paying off a debt not otherwise payable;тАФaс╣Зd it prefers the latter.

It is quoted in Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б (3.39), which adds that тАШdharmaтАЩ stands for such necessities as medication and the like.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

In connection with the prohibition of the selling of sesamum except under the said conditions, we have this declamatory statement.

тАЬIt has been declared that the mention of the wrong involved in the doing of what is forbidden is the purpose served by declamatory assertions; why then should the declamatory statement in the present ease be put forward in the formтАФтАШHe becomes a worm if he does anything else with sesamum than eating, anointing and giving?тАЩтАЭ

The answer to this is as follows:тАФThis has been asserted in this form because the result spoken of is one that is impossible and also contrary to what has been asserted in other treatises. For instance, it is said here that the man plunges into ordure тАШalong with his ancestors,тАЩтАФand certainly no wrong is committed by these ancestors; the results of good and bad acts always accrue to the man that does them; in no sense could the ancestors be the persons that did the act in question; all which has been already discussed before. Then again, it is said below (in 92) thatтАФтАШby selling meat he at once becomes an outcasteтАЩ; where becoming an out-caste could not apply to any one else except the seller himself. From all this it is clear that all that is meant to be really related to the prohibition is that something undesirable happens; and the words of the text cannot be taken as literally true. Hence what is meant is that тАШthe man who does anything elseтАФin the shape of selling and the likeтАФwith sesamum than eating and the rest, becomes a worm,тАФi.e., becomes tainted with the evil effects described.тАЩтАФ(91)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 933);тАФin Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б (3.39), to the effect that the selling of sesamum otherwise than what is mentioned in the preceding verse is sinful;тАФin Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─А c─Бra p. 431);тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 124).
